Letter Received

To the Editor: I have read your newspaper's report on the 30th of this month regarding the Huang Chu Jiu property liquidation case tried by the French Concession Court. The report on the court's decree was brief and not detailed, and there were discrepancies. Upon investigation, the court's decree on that day stated that Huang's family's representative requested to change the court's decree issued on July 18th. The plaintiff unanimously opposed it. The court found it inappropriate to change it. The two auctions should still be revoked. The liquidator and Huang's family representative requested to change the sale to a competitive sale. All parties agreed that it was beneficial and harmless. The liquidator and the representative should conduct a competitive sale together and submit a report for consideration. It was also heard that after the first auction was revoked, the buyer raised an objection. The court did not receive a request and therefore could not rule on it and should wait for a legal solution. Some creditors claimed that Huang had concealed property and requested an investigation, but no evidence was presented. The liquidator should investigate and handle the matter. Dong Shiyun, director and shareholder of the Gongfa Company, appeared in court and stated that he was unable to repay the debt. The liquidator should investigate all the shareholder's property and submit a report for consideration. As for Huang's estate report, it was based on over six million yuan. The movable property was estimated and calculated by experts from various industries. The real estate was calculated based on the current market value. The profits from rented land and buildings were estimated based on the contracted lease term of more than 20 years. All stocks, regardless of their actual value, could only be valued according to the face value. Who would have thought that today, due to the creditors' eagerness for compensation, the accountant's method of disposing of the property could not be carried out according to the original plan, and everyone would inevitably suffer losses. For example, the disposal of the Gongfa Company's various properties, when actually sold, was far less than the estimated price. The difference in loss will be as much as millions. Using that as an example, it can be determined that Huang's property cannot be sold at a fair price. Taking the rented land and buildings as an example, there was originally a profit of more than three million yuan. Now that it is being sold urgently, it is conceivable that it will not be able to obtain a considerable price. All of this was not expected at first. Now, a large portion of Huang's property has not been sold, so how can the accountant's report that it is only worth more than 1.7 million yuan be taken as a definitive conclusion? As for Huang's jewelry, it is certainly worth more than a few hundred yuan, but during Huang Chu Jiu's lifetime, he had already mortgaged tens of thousands of yuan of valuable jewelry for business operations. The amount of the mortgage and the mortgagors are all recorded in the liquidation report. How could there be any concealment? Fearing that rumors may be misrepresented, I hereby clarify. I hope you will investigate and publish it in the letter section to make corrections. Respectfully, to the Chief Editor of Shen Bao, Lawyer Tan Yigong.

Letter Received

The Problem of Implementing the Factory Law in Our Country

Chen Da

(2) Specific Discussions, Working Hours and Related Articles, 1. Young Workers: Children working in factories, between the ages of twelve and sixteen, we call young workers. Those smaller than young workers we call child laborers. However, our country currently lacks population surveys and has not adopted birth certificates, so proving age is very difficult. Therefore, our current survey does not ask about the age of children, but rather deals with the reality. There are many children in factories who, judging by their height and physique, are around ten years old. The working conditions of child laborers in many places are similar to those in the report of the Child Labor Committee (1924), but this report has had a considerable effect on public opinion. Because many new factories have gradually abolished the youngest children, and foreign-owned cotton mills (a total of thirty-four) now measure the height of children before employing them, admitting only those who meet the standard. This method of measurement has also been adopted by several Chinese-owned yarn and silk mills, but the height adopted varies. However, four feet two inches is a relatively common standard. This standard is based on the average of measurements of one thousand children. Several new-style silk reeling factories in Shanghai are gradually adopting Japanese-style cocoon boiling machines, which boil the cocoons in another room and then send them to the silk reeling workers. Therefore, the boiling work does not need to be the responsibility of child laborers. This has two benefits: the number of child laborers can naturally be reduced, and the temperature of the silk reeling room can be reduced because there is no need to boil cocoons, so the working conditions in the cocoon factory can be improved. The factory law of our country stipulates that young workers must be at least fourteen years old to work in the factory. According to the regulations for the implementation of the factory law, the method of proof is provided by the legal guardian. In practice, this kind of proof is unreliable. Generally, in order to alleviate the economic difficulties of the child's family, the guardian will definitely say that the smaller child is of legal age. There are usually several ways to prove age: 1. Proved by the child or legal guardian; 2. Determined by the employer or factory staff; 3. Determined by a judge or doctor. In India and Hong Kong, the method for young workers is mostly certified by doctors hired by the government. Before the child enters the factory, the doctor examines the body, and those who are strong are issued a permit by the doctor, and they can enter the factory to work with the certificate. Those who are not issued a certificate cannot work. The doctor also determines the age of the child, but does not pay attention to the proof of age, but pays attention to the health of the child. There are 11,895 child laborers in the six industries in Shanghai (according to the latest report of the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau, there are 27,482 child laborers in the ten industries). The most child laborers are employed in silk reeling, cotton spinning, printing, machinery, and tobacco cases. Except for foreign-owned cotton mills, which no longer use the youngest child laborers (their young workers must be at least four feet two inches tall), there are still very young child laborers in many Chinese-owned factories. However, most opinions believe that child labor should be banned. The author would like to contribute the following opinions on the method of banning: the government should appoint several doctors to examine the bodies of children, and those who are qualified will be given employment certificates. The qualified children must be a certain number of feet tall (determined after investigation) and at least twelve years old (the proof of age is not the main thing). The above methods have two difficulties: A. For children who have already been employed, another type of certificate must be issued to show the difference; B. The government must pay the cost of appointing doctors separately, but according to the experience of the United Kingdom, the cost is not very high. When doctors went to factories to check bodies in 1901, they charged two shillings and six pence for every five children, and six pence for each child from six children onwards. If children go to the doctor's clinic for examination, they will be charged six pence each. "After the second revision of the charging regulations, for every factory with more than ten children, a fee of two shillings and six pence is charged, and for those with more than one hundred, a fee of seven shillings and six pence is charged." The Hong Kong Industrial Children Ordinance was passed in 1922 and amended in 1929. When it was passed that year, children over ten years old could enter the factory to work. When it was revised, the age of children was raised to twelve years old. According to the report of the Secretary for Chinese Affairs, this amendment was not opposed by anyone, which shows that the legislation is easy to benefit workers from leniency to strictness. According to this survey, it is known that the working hours of male and female child laborers are roughly the same. However, the printing industry has special circumstances, because the workers in this industry generally do not work full shifts at night, but extend their working hours by a few hours during busy times. The average night work hours in the six industries are 9.2 hours for male workers, 8.7 hours for female workers, and 7.7 hours for child laborers. However, if the number of clock hours per shift is used as the standard, the average working hours in the six industries is 9.6 hours. The working hours in the cotton spinning industry, whether day shift or night shift, are mostly more than eleven hours. As for the number of shifts per day and night, except for the silk reeling and machinery industries, which only have one shift, most of the other industries have more than one shift. The chemical industry has 1.3 shifts per day and night, the food industry has 1.2 shifts (of which the tobacco industry has 1.02 shifts, or only a few night shifts, the cotton spinning industry has two shifts per day and night, each shift is almost twelve hours, the public utility industry has three shifts, each shift is eight hours. The above facts tell us that the ten-hour work system can be implemented in the Shanghai industry. However, the implementation of this system will cause economic losses to the textile industry (especially the cotton and silk industries). The author cannot estimate the total economic losses, because Chinese and foreign factories have not provided appropriate information on the value of products and fixed expenses. However, the economic losses suffered by the industry due to shortening working hours include at least the following three items: A. The reduction of output; B. The fixed expenses of closing the factory; C. Wages. After working hours are shortened, workers' fatigue can be reduced and work efficiency can be improved, so production is not necessarily reduced. However, this effect can only be achieved after a considerable period of time, and it is not a common phenomenon, because there are many factories whose output is based on machinery. Shortening the time means reducing production. As for the workers, whether they are paid by the hour or by the piece, most of them are unwilling to reduce their wages because of shortening working hours. As a result, the factory must at least pay the same wages as before. A small number of factories have made slight estimates of the economic losses of shortening working hours. Several cotton mills believe that reducing from twelve hours to ten hours will result in a total economic loss of 9%, of which the production volume alone will be reduced by 17%. A large-scale manufacturing plant shortened working hours (from 10:00 to 9:00) two years ago, and its total loss was 10%. According to the estimate of this factory, if it is reduced to eight hours again, the increased loss will be 12.5%. A public utility company employing 950 workers implemented an eight-hour work system two years ago, and its total loss was 8400 yuan per year. Working hours should be mentioned in the same breath as night work. Article 12 of the Factory Law of our country stipulates that child laborers shall not work between 7:00 pm and 6:00 am the next day, and Article 13 stipulates that female workers shall not work between 10:00 pm and 6:00 am the next day. In Hong Kong, child laborers under the age of fifteen are not allowed to work after 7:00 pm and before 7:00 am, and young workers under the age of eighteen are not allowed to work after 9:00 pm and before 7:00 am. In India, young workers and female workers are not allowed to work after 7:00 pm and before 5:30 am. Since the ban on late-night work in 1929, the Japanese cotton spinning industry has worked 17 hours a day and night, divided into two shifts (8.5 hours per shift). Those who use a one-shift system can extend the night work to 11:00 pm. If the factory law of our country is in accordance with the current regulations, there are only 16 hours of work per day and night, divided into two shifts. In addition to the economic losses, there are also practical difficulties. For example, the question of workers' dormitories. Most of the female workers in Japanese cotton mills have dormitories, so there is no problem in returning home after get off work at night. However, most of the female workers in Shanghai live in nearby villages. If they get off work at 10:00 pm at night, it will be difficult for female workers to return home. As for the dormitory floor, there are many shortcomings, and it seems that our country cannot imitate it. Based on the above facts and reasons, our country cannot currently implement a sixteen-hour work system per day and night, especially because international competition is fierce and the efficiency of our country's workers is too low. The author's suggestion is a ten-hour work system. For female workers and young workers, whether day or night, their working hours are ten hours. Within three years of the implementation of the factory law, the exception of the ten-hour work system for late-night work will be temporarily preserved as follows: (A) Some industries whose manufacturing work uses machinery and cannot be stopped continuously (any exception must be listed); (B) Seasonal industries (listed by enumeration, but the silk industry cannot be used as an exception); (C) Industries exclusively for male workers; (D) Those who encounter natural disasters and special incidents. Within three years, the industry should conduct in-depth research on the issue of banning late-night work, and must pay special attention to the following two things: (A) Can male workers replace female workers? Most cotton mill employers believe that this is impossible. Several cotton mills in Hunan and Hubei use male workers, but they are limited to rougher work. In Indian cotton mills, 4% of the workers are young workers, and female workers account for a small part. This situation is different from cotton mills in other countries, and it is not something that our country can imitate in a short time. A factory in Tianjin has recently implemented an eight-hour system, but it is said that this factory has always had difficulties in management. In order to alleviate the unemployment of workers, the two shifts have been changed to three shifts. Although production has increased by about 4% since the eight-hour work system was implemented, the industry strongly opposes it. Whether the new system can be successful is a question, but the relationship between labor and capital seems to have gradually improved, and night work has been reduced to ten times a month (but there is currently no confirmed report on how to change shifts at 10:00 pm at night so that female workers can return home without difficulty). Within three years, the industry should study how to avoid the unemployment of female workers or the reduction of sales after late-night work is banned. This is the question of increasing machinery. We can refer to Japan's experience. Japan spent three years preparing to abolish late-night work. We believe that the period is too long. Buying a large number of machines to avoid reducing production and reducing sales, we believe that it is too much of a concern. The facts and reasons can be found in John E. Orchard's "Japan's Economic Position". At the end of John E. Orchard's "Johan's Economic Position", there is also overtime work, and the wages are increased by one-third to two-thirds compared to the usual wages. These points seem to be consistent with the current situation and can be implemented. Regarding this issue, the author's suggestions are as follows: Child laborers are not allowed to have overtime work under any circumstances. Female workers on day and night shifts are also not allowed to have overtime work in order to protect the health of female workers and young workers. (2) Rest Days, Holidays, and Special Rest Days: Rest days, holidays, and special rest days should be discussed separately and comprehensively, because the rest and holiday conditions of various industries are different, so for the sake of clarity, they should be discussed separately. Because rest and holidays not only protect workers' health, but also reduce production, which is also part of the industry's economic losses, they should be discussed comprehensively. The factory law of our country stipulates that there is one day of rest every seven days, seven national holidays every year, and special holidays from seven to fifteen days every year (determined by the length of service of the workers). Most of these holidays must be paid. In addition, there are also relationships between holidays and reduced production, fixed expenses, etc. However, because this survey cannot collect data on these two levels, the total economic loss cannot be estimated. As for the partial losses, especially the payment of wages, can be briefly discussed as follows: (A) Rest days: In Shanghai's industries, there is generally rest time during the daily working hours, from 15 minutes for the short ones to one hour for the long ones, mostly during meals. As for the full-day rest days, the situation varies greatly. A small number of factories have no rest days in a month. Some factories adopt a work-count system. Although there are regulations on rest days on the surface, if workers work on rest days, they can get double wages. Workers are encouraged by this (especially piecework) to petition to work, so they can get more wages. Therefore, rest days exist in name only. Some industries are continuous, and their workers cannot have rest days, but their daily working hours are shorter than ordinary industries. In addition to the above situations, the remaining factories give holidays for rest days, and the number ranges from two to four days per month. According to this survey, the rest days of 176 factories are 2.6 days per month, so according to the actual situation, there are not many rest days. Although rest days are indispensable for the health of workers, the number of rest days can only be increased slowly and cannot be rushed due to the relationship between production and work efficiency. The average number of rest days per month for 176 factories is 2.6 days, of which 55 are paid and 121 are unpaid. Those who are paid are mostly factories that employ long-term workers, and they often adopt a wage increase system, for example, those who work 28 days a month get the wages of 30 days, and those who work 30 days get the wages of 33 days. Some foreign factories give the wages of 29 days to those who work 26 days a month (Sundays are not paid for rest). Rest days (and holidays) should be compared with the actual situation in other cities in our country, and then a concept can be obtained. According to the survey of 51 cities by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, there are 17 cities with more than 10,000 industrial workers in each city, of which six cities (Qingdao, Nantong, Shanghai, Wuchang, Guangzhou, Shunde) have more than 33 rest days and holidays per year, and two cities (Hankou, Yixing) have between 24 and 30 days. When Japan banned late-night work, there were four rest days per month. Since the ban on late-night work, there have only been two rest days per month. The United Kingdom has one and a half rest days per week, and India has four days per month, but most of them are unpaid. The articles in the factory law of our country regarding the payment of wages for rest days are obviously sympathizing with the workers. In order to improve their economic life, workers have recently often demanded an increase in their income, and therefore demanded the payment of wages for rest days. However, the payment of wages for rest days seems to be inconsistent with the principle. Workers should change their policy and demand an increase in wages.

The conference should investigate the cost of living in important industrial and commercial areas, and then formulate a cost of living index as a standard for setting the minimum wage. According to the factory law of our country, there are four rest days per month (i.e. 52 days per year) and eight national holidays, most of which must be paid. Judging from the payment of wages alone, the economic burden of the industry is already considerable. One factory employing 983 workers has made a calculation that it needs to pay 2565 yuan for one day of rest every seven days, and because of the continuous work, it also needs to hire an additional one-seventh of the workers on the seventh day, which is another type of expense. Cotton mills generally rest on Sundays without pay. One type of silk reeling factory believes that every Sunday rest will reduce the output by 3 loads per day, and the fixed expenses will increase by 275 taels per day (equivalent to 37.671 yuan in silver). According to this survey, the average number of holidays and holidays given by each industry each year is 32.1 days, or equal to two rest days per month and eight holidays. Therefore, we have assumed that there are two rest days per month and eight national holidays per year, which seems to be close to the actual situation. However, because the implementation of the ten-hour work has already had a significant economic impact on the industry, we believe that national holidays are paid and rest is not. Some factories (both Chinese and foreign) have gradually complied with the orders of the National Government and take holidays on commemorative days, but the situation is not consistent and the number of holidays is not uniform, ranging from one to eight days per year, but the trend is obvious, which is to follow the orders of the National Government and proceed on the one hand. This type of holiday has a considerable relationship with promoting patriotism and should be widely promoted. Some factories, in view of the difficulty of changing the customs of our country, still take holidays during the Lunar New Year in place of holidays, and this level is also in accordance with custom, and the government does not need to be too demanding. New Year's holidays are common. In summary, factories now give an average of 14.4 holidays per year, "i.e., 4.7 national holidays, 1.7 festival holidays, 3.9 New Year's holidays, and 4.1 Lunar New Year holidays." Regarding national holidays, 81 factories pay wages and 72 do not. Regarding festival holidays, 48 factories pay wages and 68 do not. Regarding Gregorian New Year's holidays, 66 factories pay wages and 107 do not. Regarding Lunar New Year's holidays, 31 factories pay wages and 91 do not. Since the actual situation is as described above, our suggestions for rest days and holidays are as follows: Eight national holidays are given each year with pay for the following reasons: This issue must take into account the health of workers and industrial production. If it is exclusively for the sake of health, the more rest days, the better, of course. However, for the country as a whole, the current rest days and holidays are still very few, as described above, so we can only temporarily set two days per month, plus eight national holidays per year. As far as rest days are concerned, they can be increased to four days per month after five years. As for the issue of production, international competition must be discussed. There are 190 large-scale Japanese factories in South Manchuria, and their average number of rest days per month is only 2.2 days. The degree of industrialization in Osaka is very high, but for 170 large-scale factories, the average number of rest days per month is only 2.9 days. The degree of industrialization in our country is immature, and the efficiency of workers is relatively low. If we add rest days and holidays, production will be even lower. How can we compete with foreign industries? In practice, there is no precedent for paying wages for holidays in foreign countries, and it seems to be a sound reason in principle. However, we believe that paying wages for national holidays has the good intention of promoting patriotism and can be implemented. Regarding the issue of workers demanding an increase in income, we should request the government to conduct scientific research on wages and living expenses as soon as possible in order to implement appropriate solutions. According to the factory law, 60 days of paid leave are given each year, and the cost is very high, but some factories now pay wages for holidays (commemorative days or festival holidays). One factory employing 55 employees believes that the wages for eight holidays will be 5900 yuan. However, if some of the current paid holidays are replaced, the increased cost will only be 1500 yuan. Cotton mills generally do not pay wages for holidays, so the wages for eight holidays will increase the total cost by 3%. In short, the current average number of rest days is 2.6 days per month, and the average number of holidays is 14.4 days per year. We believe that the factory law can stipulate that there are two rest days per month without pay, and eight national holidays per year with pay, which is equivalent to one-seventh of the cost of 60 days of holidays in the factory law.) Because the wage issue is fundamental, after the government has conducted considerable research on this issue, it will then study the issue of rest days and holidays in conjunction. Special rest days: In India and our country, there are often many workers who leave their hometowns to make a living. The people of both countries attach great importance to the concept of their hometown, so the method in India often gives workers the opportunity to return home to visit their families within a year, but without pay. The factory law of our country also has special holiday regulations in order to cater to the social ideas of the people of our country. The annual holidays are set from seven to fifteen days with pay, based on the length of service of the workers. The newly opened factories are not affected by this article. If the more historical factories have records of the length of service of workers, they feel that this is a huge economic burden. For example, one factory employing 567 people estimates the special holidays as follows: those who have worked for one to three years get seven days of leave, totaling 400 yuan; those who have worked for three to five years get ten days of leave, totaling 1700 yuan; those who have worked for five to ten years get fourteen days of leave, totaling 11600 yuan; those who have worked for more than ten years get fifteen days of leave, totaling 4400 yuan. One factory employing 225 employees estimates the cost of special holidays to be 6000 yuan per year. One factory with a staff of 601 people has the following expenses for special rest days: 167 people get seven days of leave per year, totaling 970 yuan; 76 people get ten days of leave per year, totaling 750 yuan; 214 people get fourteen days of leave per year, totaling 2850 yuan; 144 people get fifteen days of leave per year, totaling 2400 yuan. A large-scale factory with a total of 9300 workers estimates the cost of special holidays to be 107,000 yuan per year.

Free Talk

World News in Brief

— Sea Guest

The Fisherman Reaps the Benefit

The shipowner of the British Aukra Com Pany, Yin Baila Zeng Cap Lngrightsen, recently caught a whale. The profit he made was more than a hundred times that of an ordinary whale. He really reaped the benefit of the fisherman. An ordinary whale can produce oil from its fat worth four hundred pounds, while the one Yin Baila Zeng got can be worth forty thousand pounds. The whale is not very big, and the fat production is naturally not much different from ordinary whales. However, the sailors suddenly cheered with great joy when they were cutting it open. It turned out that they had found a large piece of shapeless yellow material, weighing more than a hundred pounds. Do you know what this yellow material is? It turned out to be the extremely precious ambergris in the world. The price of each tael is twenty pounds, which is five times more expensive than gold. This kind of ambergris is extremely needed by manufacturers of perfume. No matter what kind of fragrance the perfume is made of, if ambergris is added to it, the fragrance will never fade. It had only been found twice in whales before, and the area was larger than this one. This is the third time. It is said that the whale's usual food is squid in the sea, and ambergris is produced from the sharp beak of the squid.

Talks from a Northeastern Returnee

— Holding a Buddha

A guest returned from Harbin and met him at the inn. He spoke of many trivial matters in the Northeast. Today, the Wanbaoshan case is causing a sensation across the country. I will record it hastily, not only to help the conversation. The guest said: Manchuria is located between the two major forces of Japan and Russia. It is not easy for the person in power to deal with the situation. The Japanese are especially insidious and malicious in their long-term plans. Japan only has 43,700 square miles with 85 million people, while Manchuria has 650,000 square miles with only 28 million people. Therefore, they are working hard to promote the policy of immigration and colonization, moving Japanese to Korea, and Koreans moving to Manchuria. The occurrence of this Wanxian tragedy is a clear proof of the Japanese policy of immigration and colonization. According to the Chinese farmers in the East, most of them came from the Denglai area of Shandong. They are diligent and hardworking, and are often jealous of by the Japanese and Koreans. Many have become rich households from scratch, but they lack a long-term vision and a spirit of mutual assistance. This is a shortcoming of ordinary Chinese people, which cannot be denied. However, the Japanese are not like this. There is a wealthy household who specializes in lending money to Korean farmers, and has won the favor of the Korean farmers, so they can be used without knowing it. This is another reason for the tragedy. There are bandits all over the Eastern Province, who are extremely fierce. After sunset in Harbin, the whole city closes its doors. It is like walking on thorns. No one dares to step out. However, the Japanese ronin are all familiar with the bandits. Therefore, although the bandits are fierce, the Japanese can play with them in their hands. Otherwise, how could the Japanese be so rampant? In Japan, not only the intellectual class knows the way to love the country, but also the ronin. They are far beyond what the bandits can match. However, the bandits are also very cunning. Last winter, a village was attacked by bandits. The villagers built a fort to defend themselves. The bandits could not succeed. One day, several people came carrying a coffin, seemingly wanting to bury it beside the fort. The villagers came out to stop them, not knowing that they had fallen into their trap. With a loud shout, several people took out guns from the coffin and broke into the fort, and were robbed. It turned out to be the bandits who had failed before. The bandits are good at riding and shooting, and so are the residents. A bandit came out of a house fully loaded with loot. Suddenly, there was a loud bang, and three bandits fell to the ground one after another. The remaining bandits did not know where the bullets came from, and scattered like birds and beasts. Only afterwards did they know that the family who had been robbed had a daughter who was only nine years old. Seeing the bandits coming out, she hid behind the window and shot the bandits with a gun. She killed them. Those who heard it admired the little girl's wisdom and courage. The guest also said that the Eastern Province is rich in forests and gold mines, and is indeed a land of abundance. For example, the Yitong River and the Songhua River area have fertile land everywhere, which is suitable for rice, and everything else is suitable for wheat. Is this why the Japanese are so greedy?

Hot Topics in Cold Records

— Songlu

The scorching sun is rampant. The stifling heat traps people. A guest has just arrived from Hangzhou. His breathing hasn't settled. Sweat pours like ink. He urgently asks for ice cream to relieve the heat. He finishes one cup and asks for more. I smile and say, "Guest, please be patient. Allow me to tell you how to dispel the heat." The guest agrees. So, I turn on an electric fan, prepare melon and fruit, and order a servant to fully open the water tap in the next room. I solemnly tell him, "It's raining." The guest says, "Really? I knew it was going to rain." I say, "Is the heat reduced now?" The guest is leafing through a book on the table. He slowly replies, "The weather is unpredictable. But for the time being, it is much cooler." I clap my hands and stand up, saying, "Indeed! The power of psychology is amazing." Then I tell him that I lied about the rain. The heat and coolness are only due to the change in psychology. The guest is speechless and laughs. I say, "Looking at plums can quench thirst. Can hearing about ice not dispel heat? Let's each tell a cold joke to relieve the heat. What do you think?" The guest nods. I imitate Chunyu's story and say:

Last New Year's Eve, I was traveling in Hangzhou. It was very cold at the time. Snow fell three feet deep. I rode with my girlfriend, Hua Ying, to the western suburbs. Accidentally, we lost control. The horse would not move forward. I hit it with my hand. The horse jumped up. I fell to the ground face-first in the snow. My face was perfectly imprinted. Ying was shocked. She quickly asked if I was hurt. I laughed and said, "No harm done. But this trip is so much fun. It should be recorded. So, I imitated the ancient people's idea of snow mud and swan footprints. I left a shadow in the snow as a souvenir."

After I finished speaking, the guest laughed loudly. When he stopped laughing, he imitated Manqian's story and said, "The winter before last, Hangzhou was very cold. The shallow parts of West Lake were frozen to the bottom. Boats could not move. Residents in the Lakeside Pavilion could not reach the shore for days. They were about to starve. So, an adventurer stepped on the ice to walk. Unexpectedly, before he reached the halfway point, the ice suddenly broke. He fell into the water. Luckily, there were huge ice blocks on both sides, solid and thick. He was submerged to his shoulders. He floated on the surface of the water and did not die. The people on the shore saw it and could not help him. Later, a strong and powerful man threw him a pole. He grabbed the pole with his hand and was pulled up. Afterwards, a joker asked him, 'Was the ice-running game fun?' He laughed and replied, 'Nothing special. I was just imitating Wang Xiang's lying on the ice to seek carp!'"

As soon as the guest finished speaking, laughter filled the room. One person stood up and said, "The guest's story is interesting. Let me try to tell one to add to the fun. What do you think?" Everyone said, "Good." That person said, "One year, it was extremely cold. The temperature dropped below zero. An old-fashioned scholar usually liked to buy Japanese goods and criticized young people's patriotism as unnecessary. That day, he was about to smoke his water pipe. Unexpectedly, the water in the pipe was frozen. He was about to call a servant to change the water. But the saliva on his mouth froze to the pipe and could not be removed. The old-fashioned scholar could not open his mouth. He was extremely embarrassed and cried. As soon as the tears flowed on his face, they froze into ice. Later, someone saw it and pulled it off for him. But with too much force, he lost a tooth. Blood trickled down. In an instant, the blood also turned into ice. One person mocked him and said, 'This is truly a cold-blooded animal!'"

Before he finished speaking, the room was noisy. At that time, a cool breeze suddenly arrived. The sweltering heat disappeared. The guest put on his clothes and said goodbye. He said, "Tonight's conversation is much better than eating snow pears and ice lotus roots." I sent the guest back. Then I took up my pen to record it.

A note to contributors to the Lake Pavilion Poetry Class: Thank you for sending your manuscripts. The deadline was yesterday. We have compiled and sent them for review. We will no longer accept submissions. Once the selection is completed, we will disclose the best ones. I hereby notify you. Tianxu Wosheng

▲News from the publishing world: The "Military Medicine" edited and printed by the Capital Military Medical Students Association has now been published to the sixth issue. This issue is rich in content. It selects many specialized treatises on military medicine. In particular, the article "The Early Development History of Military Medicine in Our Country" written by Wu Yubai narrates the historical facts of military medicine in our country during the Guangxu period, which is very detailed. It collects various precious and secret historical materials. In addition, there are also "Sequelae of Dysentery in Combatants" submitted by Teng Yiqi, a military doctor studying in Germany, and "Personality Research of Aviation Soldiers" by Lu Xinjiu, etc., all of which are extremely sophisticated professional papers. In addition to more than ten articles of treatises and translations, there are also miscellaneous notes, etc. The price is thirty cents. The consignment offices are the Military Medical Students Association in Dongguan, Nanjing, or the Military Medical Bulletin Society in Sitiao Lane.

I Will Be a Fish

— Tianjian

For the past ten days, there have been violent winds and torrential rains. It happens several times a day. The crops north and south of the Yangtze River have been devastated by floods. The decision of the Huai River and the overflow of the Yangtze River, and the farmers who build dikes and die with their bodies, is heard every day. Alas, I will be a fish! I write a song, "I Will Be a Fish." The song says: I will be a fish. Why is Heaven so cruel? The sea is overturned, the earth's axis shifts, and the divine tortoise escapes. Wuzhi breaks the lock, Tian Wu spreads. The demon cloud seems to swallow the red sun. Twenty days of heavy rain and thunder. The white day is dark, like a mute room. The rain flows like ropes and threads. The water floods the flat ground and the ditches are lost. The Huai and Si rivers flow rapidly and break the long dikes. The Yangtze River and the Grand Canal surge with waves. The farmers do not take off their raincoats day and night. Men, women, old, and young are frightened. They build dikes in the middle of the night to defend against Feng Yi. The rain is heavy, the water is fierce, and the effort is difficult. They grab the ground and call to Heaven, but Heaven does not respond. Their bodies are swept away by the waves and disappear. East and west fields are no longer distinguishable. Seventy percent of the fertile land is lost. The Beijing-Shanghai road is flooded and the cars cannot pass. The Tianjin-Pukou road is submerged and also closed. My hometown is low-lying and even more worrying. We only have one harvest after several years. The warehouses and granaries are not yet empty. But how can such a huge disaster be enough to support us? This morning, I suddenly saw the sun shining. But the wind is strong and the rain is heavier at night. The wind is strong and the rain is heavier at night. We cannot avoid becoming fish.

Travel Notes of India (71)

— Linghua

I think, can the power of the British defeat the German army but not the unarmed Indians? This is a big question. But I think there are five reasons why Gandhi's methods are partially effective. The first is the national movement. The relationship between England and India is like the relationship between the Manchus and the Han Chinese in the past. Second, India is completely blockaded. There is no way to obtain military equipment. There is no other way but the unarmed movement. Therefore, this emotional hypnosis technique is invented out of desperation. Everything is created by coercion. Third, there are too many Indians and too few British. No matter what, the British cannot kill too many people in such a big country. Fourth, Indian philosophy and culture are high. It is easy to tend towards gentle movements. Fifth, since the Great War, Britain's internal strength has declined. It is not as arrogant as it used to be. With these five reasons, Gandhi's movement should be partially successful. If, as the Indians say, they rely solely on unarmed movements, they can cut off the British military expenditure, give up the government, and give them independence and freedom, like the British did to the United States. I am afraid it will not be easy to do. It is too optimistic. I firmly believe in dynamics. But there has never been such a miracle. Those who overthrow the government with bare hands, I think there will be a day. It will still solve the problem of strength through changes in the army. Gandhi's movement is just the flower. If you want to pick the fruit, you must use arm strength. The hopes of the Indians today, we still cannot fully believe.

A student named Shiridaha is young and good at talking. He said that his ancient civilization was very high. According to the Vedic classics, India had airships and machinery as early as 4000 BC. It was only due to the decline of culture in the middle that the new learning revived today and the ancient learning also revived. In the future, it will definitely be able to dominate the world. Our Indian culture is in the world, not in one country. I couldn't believe it. The Indians could build airships in 4000 BC. But if we compare it with Western history and Chinese books, it is not unreasonable. According to the famous H.G. Wells's The Outline of History, there was a Cretan race before the Greeks, who were a very civilized people. The Greeks once inherited their culture. The Cretans once built airships. It is not without basis. Like the Chinese Gongshuban and Mozi, who both built wooden kites, these are all believable. Because Luban and Mozi are people known to everyone, not mysterious talks. I have traveled to various provinces in China and Southeast Asia. There are Luban temples everywhere. Because of the relationship between craftsmanship, evolution is very large. And today's era of workers, I very much hope that teachers in various parts of China will promote elementary school students to study the Luban Sutra. There are several Luban Sutras. Each bookstore sells them. They are used by carpenters. There are pictures and dimensions. It talks about the method of building wooden utensils and houses. All craftsmen regard it as the Bible. I once looked at it. I didn't pay attention to it at the time. Now I feel its importance. It is the essence of ancient craftsmanship. I am afraid that Chinese workers have too little knowledge. There are places where they have reversed their books. But even small pieces of it are very precious. The word "showing off one's skill before Luban" can spread its culture. The ancient Indian books have the wisdom of craftsmanship. The era of its airship invention is earlier than Greece and China. There may be some truth to it. But Indian mythology is difficult to fully believe. Or it is an ideal. But several students told me solemnly that it was recorded in the classics. It should not be a lie. It is a pity that the good historian H.G. Wells did not hear this. The student also said that the ancient Vedic scriptures are not complete now. It is very difficult to read. Even Indian scholars find it difficult to understand. This student is very erudite. According to others, his father is a famous leader of a political movement. He is very knowledgeable.

Rotary Club Speaking

Women Women (6)

— Yao Su Feng

His mother thought that he was complaining about the noodles not being cooked well. She even asked him in a nagging way if he wanted her to buy something outside. Finally, she peeled a few of the bananas that he had brought back for him to eat. She felt that this was very unfair to her son.

She kept nagging and talking to her son, but he didn't really hear a word of it. His wife stood silently to the side, also feeling that she had many important things to say, but regretting that she didn't have the opportunity now.

He finally explained his intention for coming back. His family then realized that he had come back specifically to take money out.

His father, who had been sitting quietly for a long time, suddenly showed the most serious expression. "What should we do? We might be able to figure something out by the time school starts, but why do we have to pay in advance now?" His father said worriedly.

"How much money do you need in total?" His mother also asked helplessly.

"It's not much money, one hundred and sixty yuan is enough." He slightly raised his head that was drooping down and looked at his wife out of the corner of his eye.

His wife also felt unable to help, and just felt very sorry for him. The room was suddenly filled with a gloomy atmosphere, gradually leading to intermittent sighs.

"How could a family like ours be able to afford to send a son to school? For one person to study, almost three people have to starve to death; in the end, it's all because we've suffered enough from this rickshaw-pulling job, so we foolishly fantasize about saving money and food to let Xiao Rong go to school. But this kind of foreign school, as soon as the holidays are over, demands some kind of fee in advance. Even if we go bankrupt, we won't be able to come up with it!" His father said, almost bursting into tears. He secretly cried out in agony to himself.

His mother couldn't bear to hear it anymore. She seemed to say in a comforting way... "There's no other way! Now that we've embarked on this path, we have to give it a try. It's no wonder that they collect some kind of fee in advance. Think about it, doesn't the county government also collect three years' worth of taxes in advance? Now, we can only discuss a solution properly to let Xiao Rong take it. This is originally the capital we've invested, and we'll always get a whole batch back in the future."

Finally, his wife thought of a way to help out in an emergency. She bravely said... "Father-in-law and mother-in-law, there's no need to worry! I think, as long as Xiao Rong studies hard, he'll always have a chance to make a name for himself in the future. Now, to get one hundred and sixty yuan, let's all pool together what we have! When I married into this family, didn't I still have a pair of gold bracelets? Along with the spare change I've saved from selling flowers, it should add up to more than a hundred yuan. As long as mother-in-law can put her gold jewelry in with it, we'll have the one hundred and sixty yuan."

Grains and Rice Market: Riverbank Rice Market Becomes Quiet and Active

▲South Market

Yesterday's supplies from various traders in the South Market were scarce, and inventory was also low. Today's decline may bring changes. The previous market slump and the continued price increases for imported rice by traders from other regions have slightly increased investor interest. However, transactions are only slightly more active, and this situation has led to a stable and rising market. As a result, the price of thick japonica rice has rebounded by 0.03 to 0.04 yuan (dollars), and medium-quality rice has risen slightly. The floods in the Yangtze River region will undoubtedly affect incoming ships. High-quality Lu Yang and Tip Rice are scarce, and prices have risen by 0.02 to 0.03 yuan. Second-grade rice is not coveted, and the market is tight. Glutinous rice has weakened, and sales are slow. The market is stable. Traders are still unable to obtain imported rice in sufficient quantities.

▲Xinzha

The rice market shows no signs of recovery, as there are still river stocks available, but supplies are extremely scarce towards the end of the lunar month. Firms are routinely closing their accounts, so the market is not very active. Prices for various types of rice have limited fluctuations. The prices of thick japonica and thin indica rice have risen by 0.03 yuan, while early rice is unpopular, and prices are stable. Lu Yang and Tip Rice continue to sell well in the local area, and the market is gradually tightening. River factory goods are being opened at prices of 2,000 to 3,000 dan.

▲52 Carloads of Wheat Delivered

All July wheat contracts were settled yesterday, totaling 52 carloads. It is reported that Runde delivered 13 carloads, Yutai 5 carloads, and Dingtai 12 carloads. The rest were delivered by various small traders. The recipients were also traders, with Tairun receiving 30 carloads and Xinfeng over 10 carloads. The rest were small traders. After the floodwaters recede in various places, there will be no shortage of goods in Shanghai. Imported wheat has also been trading briskly recently. Yesterday, two factories ordered three ships of Australian wheat at a combined price of only 4.23 taels per unit.

Silk and Tea Market: French Firms Replenish Stocks of Dried Filature Silk Due to Shortages

The silk market in Shanghai remained sluggish yesterday. There was no change in the overseas telegrams for yellow and white filature silk, and foreign exchange rates were stable. Only French firms replenished their stocks of dried filature silk, with Dachang and others importing 25 bales of Qili dried filature silk, and prices remained firm.

Scarcity of Wuxi White Filature Silk Shipments to Shanghai

Yesterday (July 31) was the final delivery day for July foreign firm futures silk contracts. Sales of white filature silk to the United States have been stagnant for a long time, and the number of sales to England and France is also very limited. Most firms require spot goods. As a result, the delivery volume of white filature silk futures for this month has been very low. The amount of silk shipped to Shanghai from Wuxi factories is very small. As of yesterday, the total amount of silk shipped to Shanghai from Wuxi factories was only around 200 bales.

North-South Goods: Orchid and Bamboo Branch Land Prices Rise by Seven Yuan

▲Dark Leaf Branches Rise by Ten Yuan

The price of orchid and bamboo branches has risen by another six or seven yuan, and dark leaf branches have risen by ten yuan. The supply is becoming increasingly scarce. Yesterday, the China Merchants Bureau's "Tunan" ship arrived with over 500 boxes, of which over 100 boxes were for transshipment. Therefore, only over 400 boxes were available in Shanghai. The price of the land, combined, requires 56 taels per box, so quotations are bound to increase further. Quanyuan red branches also arrived yesterday and were immediately offered for sale at a price of around 65 taels. The trend is stable and bullish.

Hardware: UK and US Plain Galvanized Iron Sales Advance Sharply

▲Market Overview

Yesterday's hardware transactions were good for traders from Yantai and Tianjin in the north, and procurement was also extensive in the Yangtze River region, so the trend was good. However, after the boycott, sales of UK and US plain galvanized iron have been very strong. Japanese goods can only be sold at retail in stores, and export prospects can be said to be completely cut off.

UK Galvanized Iron Inventory Emptied

Due to strong demand, the market inventory of UK galvanized iron, which had been stocked for many days, was emptied. Market conditions are very strong. 48-sheet iron is selling for 16.5 taels, 38-sheet iron for 16.75 taels, 33-sheet iron for 15.8 taels, and 25-sheet iron for 15.25 taels. It is reported that over 600-700 dan were sold in the market yesterday.

▲US Galvanized Iron Trend Improving

The US galvanized iron trade has also shown signs of improvement recently. Although there is no immediate prospect of a boom in the standard product, it is already higher than before by more than a few cents. 48-sheet iron is selling for 19.25 taels, 38-sheet iron for 19.5 taels, 33-sheet iron for 18.75 taels, and 25-sheet iron for 17.9 taels.

▲UK Steel Plate Trend Stronger

Traders from Niuzhuang, Dalian, and Tianjin bought UK steel plates yesterday, and the market outlook is optimistic. Because various traders are actively buying, there is no fear of oversupply, but the market is good, so there have been no announcements of price increases.

Youth Garden

Third-Class VIPs and Others

— Dou Mei

The last two days have been beyond my wildest dreams. Unconsciously, I have become a VIP. I have traveled between Shanghai and Hangzhou four times. However, this VIP of mine is, after all, a bit different from the ordinary so-called VIPs. The ordinary so-called VIPs, at the very least, travel in first-class cars or sleeper cars or special cars, while this VIP of mine only travels in third class. Well, then I might as well give myself a title: "A third-class VIP." Furthermore, if we talk about the essence of a VIP, the reason why a VIP is called a VIP is that what he travels for and engages in are important matters. What I did, however, was something like a tea errand. What's so important about that? But stepping back, if this matter could only be done by me, then I am clearly a VIP again. So, looking at it this way, I still don't lose my status as a VIP, only I can't get rid of a prefix — "third-class."

The day before yesterday, I was asked by a person who has several relationships with us — relative, fellow villager, classmate of my younger brother, and also his friend — Mr. Ding, to register for Zhejiang University. Originally, registration could be done by mail in Shanghai, but this rule had been discontinued the day before — the 14th. Therefore, I had to "eat dragon meat and personally go into the sea." If Mr. Ding really had to register in person, then on the one hand, he would need to prepare his lessons and couldn't run around at will; on the other hand, he wasn't very familiar with traveling. In this way, it seemed that only I could fulfill this obligation. Asking someone else, in this hot weather, who would be happy to take on this errand? So, without waiting for Mr. Ding to open his mouth, I boldly volunteered.

I planned to take the 7:10 train. At 6:20, I stood at the bus stop waiting for the bus. Who knew that more than five buses passed by, but none of them went to the North Station? This really made me anxious. At this time, it was absolutely too late to call a rickshaw, because the first train arrived at 1:00. I wanted to catch the 2:00 train back that day. If I had to sacrifice this train, I would really be unwilling in my heart. My eyes were anxiously looking north, and the police officer next to the station (because I met him every time I waited for the bus, he seemed to be an acquaintance already) kept telling me what time it was, which made me even more anxious. Finally, I didn't miss the train and arrived at the North Station with ten minutes to spare. The whole way really made me angry. The carriage was packed with people. I don't know how I carelessly sat next to a woman who had three children. On the right was a burly man with a northern appearance. Of course, it was inconvenient for me to squeeze in that direction. My body was always leaning to the left, but that woman was clearly unhappy and deliberately squeezed towards me, intending to push me out. But I guessed her intention and deliberately didn't adjust my position. However, I suffered enough from the troubles of those three children, who were climbing up and down all the time, eating this and that. The woman was traveling with seven or eight other people in a row, both men and women, young and old. From their clothes, actions, and conversation, I concluded that they were not upper-class people. Later, the woman simply took off her coat and wore only a small, buttoned shirt, busy playing with the children and constantly stuffing melons, eggs, bread, etc. into her mouth. Another man traveling with them always wore a ferocious and hateful smile, constantly praising the current material civilization.

"It's really funny. People nowadays are simply living gods, able to soar through the clouds and ride the fog. In the morning, they are in Shanghai, and immediately they can be in Hangzhou. Damn it, as long as you have money. Also, it's easy to fight wars now. Transporting guns and troops, wow, you can travel hundreds of miles a day..."

Beginning with "damn it" and ending with "wow," he spoke with great satisfaction and relish. The other few were smoking cigarettes, eating melon seeds, and listening attentively, gradually nodding to express their admiration for the argument he had made.

How pitiful, ah, China's material civilization. Where is it? Apart from these few railways and navigable waterways, most of the rest is still mules, oxcarts, and single-wheeled human-powered vehicles on land, and sailing ships powered by manpower on waterways. Of course, they don't know how convenient the material civilization and transportation of European and American countries are. But they also live in the same place as us, and only a slight difference in the level of knowledge has made them complete frogs in a well. At that time, I didn't find their stupid words laughable, but instead, I felt an infinite sense of nameless emotion and shock. At the same time, I thought of the cliché "contentment brings happiness." They have already expressed great satisfaction with China's material life, so he has the above praise.

After registering, I barely made it to the station, but the 2:08 train had already left without me. I felt very disappointed. If I missed this train, I wouldn't have another one until 6:00. How would I spend these four hours? I was only discussing in my mind: "Oh, didn't Mom tell me a long time ago, 'Hangzhou baskets are good. Buy me two covered, tightly woven baskets to hold water chestnuts, etc. They dry well and won't rot, and mice can't get to them.'" Ah, Mom's kind instructions immediately reappeared in my mind, so I made up my mind. First, I would go to a restaurant to eat, and then hire a car to sit in Lakeside Park for a while.

"From another place."

"Imported goods."

"Not local."

"Outsider."

Sitting in Lakeside Park for less than a quarter of an hour, waves of those shady men walked past me in groups of threes and fives, muttering to themselves. You say they are hooligans, I wouldn't dare to say for sure. If they aren't, why are they so bored? The women who passed by didn't grumble anything, but they also put on a fascinated look to stare at me. The vendors all came to compete and ask me to buy things. As a result, I became annoyed. They seemed to see that I was unfamiliar and deliberately came to bully me. I had no choice but to say goodbye to that lovely West Lake girl earlier.

The baskets were bought, and the clock told me it was only 4:30. If I went to the station now, I would be laughed at. So I went to buy an umbrella, deliberately bargaining with the old man and talking nonsense in order to delay some time. As a result, I didn't spend a penny. Indeed, my mind was not on the wine. Fortunately, it wasn't a busy street, and with the shop owner's permission, I simply sat there and read the recent short story monthly.

What a blessed appearance, truly worthy of being the wife of a VIP. I couldn't help but secretly praise her.

A large line of police officers was displayed in the station like a meat screen. The captain (?) issued very solemn and heavy commands from time to time, and the police officers followed the commands to stand at attention to the left and right. I couldn't guess why they were doing this. Suddenly, the captain's command became even louder, and the police officers followed the command and stood up straight, focusing their minds. Then two guards protected a group of people who came out, all of whom were neatly dressed — to put it neurotically, their appearance also seemed neat. Among them, there was only one female guest. This female guest was extremely plump. On her white lotus-like arm, she wore a jade bracelet with a round inside and a square outside. Of course, it was the focus of our attention. At this time, the eyes of all the passengers waiting in the station were focused on that group of neat people, especially the lady. Needless to say, this was the departure of a certain VIP. From clusters of whispers, I learned that the VIP was Jiang Zuobin, and the lady was of course his wife. However, the lady's blessed appearance still remains in my mind, leaving a deep sketch.

The next morning, my younger brother came to my dormitory to discuss with me. Another person whose relationship with us was no less than that of Mr. Ding also wanted to apply to Zhejiang University, but I had to go to register them again. Although my younger brother was afraid that I would be overworked, I could not refuse the request, and I finally agreed. This is what made me this VIP.

"They came from Shanghai on the early train for two days in a row," I walked into the school's registration office, and the staff was whispering like this. After hearing this, I really didn't know what to think. The 2:00 train had obviously passed, so I got the consent of a teacher at the school and took out the work I had planned to do — to write a manuscript of random notes — in a corner of the office.

When I got back to the station, I couldn't see the police officers' meat screen anymore. However, the scene in front of the station last night immediately floated into my mind again, reminding me that it was the departure of a VIP.

Youth Garden Submission Guidelines

(1) The text should be about discussions on youth issues, news about domestic and foreign schools or students, essays, descriptions of school life, casual notes, and must not be directed at anyone.

(2) Photography is limited to youth issues.

(3) Photos about youth life (such as sports, travel, sightseeing, drama performances, various competitions, etc.), school news, and youth movements, etc. are acceptable. Individual and group photos are welcome. Do not separate the photos with two columns.

(4) The number of words in each article should not exceed 2,000.

(5) Write horizontally and do not write sloppily. Save Western text where possible. If it is necessary to cite the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

Whether or not submissions are published, they will not be returned. If you need them to be returned,

Social News

The World's Largest Post Office

— Junshan

Will Be Built in Chicago

The world's largest post office will be built in Chicago, USA. The building will occupy 50 acres, that is, more than 300 Chinese acres. It will be twelve stories high and will be completed within a year and a half. Its internal facilities can process 19 million letters and newspaper packages a day, not included. According to statistics, the size of the mail it handles in a year is just as big as the building.

Judging from its equipment, it is more appropriate to say that it is a factory than a post office. Every minute, cars collecting letters from various mailboxes come in. The collected letters are immediately sent to the top floor by elevator. By the time it falls to the lower floor, it has already been stamped, sorted, packed, and prepared to be sent out.

The internal machinery is all the latest type. Except for the parts that require the use of the brain, it is entirely machine work.

Female Leader in San Francisco's Printing Industry

— Zhu Yuxiang

An American Woman of Business Talent, Who Struggled from Nothing to Her Current Position

When Mrs. Mary Macken was forcibly dismissed by her employer, looking back on her nineteen years of arduous service, all her efforts seemed to vanish like flowing water, and her heart was filled with depression and nowhere to vent. What a painful and pitiful situation! However, now she is immersed in happiness every day, because today she has become a leading figure in the San Francisco printing industry, and has independently established a large-scale printing company. Her struggle for success is glorious and valuable, and extremely worthy of boasting to others. In San Francisco, Mrs. Mary Macken is practically the first woman to use her own private funds to run a large business, and not inherit it from her father, husband, or brothers.

It was twenty-four years ago when a young woman traveled a long distance from Meien, Poland, to California in the United States to seek her fortune. At that time, her only commercial experience was sitting at home, writing advertising copy and drawing pictures. In a city as large as San Francisco, Mrs. Mary Macken was very poor and had no acquaintances. Fortunately, she soon found a printing company near her residence, and then applied for a small position in that company. At that time, the salary was six US dollars per week.

Years passed like flowing water. Mrs. Mary Macken had become an American citizen. Her salary also gradually and steadily increased. Finally, in addition to her regular salary, the company also gave her an extra allowance each year.

At the same time, she was also elected as the first female member of the San Francisco Chamber of Commerce, receiving a generous monthly public fee. In this way, her income increased a lot, and it could be compared to the huge amount that any American woman could earn. However, the manager of the company gradually became jealous of her and soon dismissed her ruthlessly, even though she had a remarkable record of nineteen years there.

In extreme grief and resentment, Mrs. Mary Macken forced herself to pull herself together. She resolutely gathered her past savings and planned to start her own printing company. She purchased a large three-story building as the factory site. The printing machines were all the latest models, and all other equipment was also exceptionally perfect. A sign was hung outside the door that read, "Mary Macken Printing Company."

Due to her profound reputation and rich experience in the printing industry over the past nineteen years, coupled with a very agile skill, the business of Macken Printing Company had reached an extremely developed stage in just five years. The various businesses accepted daily, from business cards and movie brochures to hardcover books, were all-encompassing. Therefore, today in the United States, when people talk about the printing industry in San Francisco, no one does not know Mrs. Mary Macken, and in fact, she is indeed a female leader in the San Francisco printing industry.

In the midst of her busy schedule, in addition to striving to develop the company's business, she also took time to devote herself to social undertakings. Today, there is a vast prairie at the foot of the Sea Cliff Mountains in the suburbs of San Francisco, which is specially used as a camping site for children in the city during the holidays. Although it is nominally a municipal public property, in fact, several years ago, Mrs. Mary Macken funded the purchase of the land, developed it, and then donated it as municipal property. This is her contribution to the entertainment of children in the city.

In addition, she is also the Minister of the California Business and Professional Women's Club. At the same time, she also holds extremely important positions in the Women's Suffrage League and the National Women's Federation. Not many years ago, the American Young Women's Christian Association (YWCA) specially sent her to China to conduct a social survey. She obtained a lot of new information about the current situation of Chinese women and children, which she contributed to her own country.

Book and Newspaper Introductions

Practical Bank Correspondence

— Ling Feng

Written by Hu Zhifan

Correspondence is a specialized skill in literature, and commercial correspondence is even more unique in style. Even talented and unrestrained writers may feel unable to write a simple letter for a shop. As for bank correspondence, it is even more absolutely specialized. There are many terms used in bank business that are not understandable to outsiders.

In the Chinese publishing industry, apart from the Qiushui Xuan Correspondence, which is for private use, there are very few books on commercial correspondence. The reason for this is that Chinese businessmen only feel that writing letters is a troublesome and unimportant matter. They cherish ink like gold and are reluctant to write easily unless absolutely necessary. They do not understand that commercial letters, in addition to their mission of conveying facts, can also attract many unfamiliar customers in the world. Therefore, the correspondence departments in stores in Europe and the United States occupy a very important position in the entire store. They do not have to meet the customer in person, and a piece of paper with eight lines is enough to entice buyers to appreciate their goods.

They understand the importance of doing business by mail (Doing Business By Mail), so they strive to study the organization of commercial correspondence, how to make it simple and clear, and not to bore customers with endless chatter, while at the same time writing it with strength and interest. To meet this need, commercial correspondence publications have sprung up and become an important course in business schools.

However, those are all ordinary commercial letters, only suitable for department stores. There is still nothing specifically about banking business. The author of this book, in view of the development of Chinese banks and the urgent need for such works, based on his experience, wrote this book. It contains one hundred simple and fluent English letters. All the letters that occur in daily banking business can be considered to be fully prepared. Among them, deposits, pledges, import and export, telegraphic transfers, etc., are classified into categories, and each letter is practical and can be used as a blueprint for bankers. It is also a must-read book for commercial students studying banking. Taking advantage of the book's reprint, I am specially introducing it in a few words. Sales agencies: Commercial Press, Qunyi Bookstore, Civilization Bookstore, etc. in various ports.

Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Introduction Manuscripts

(1) The text is limited to introducing the latest domestic and foreign publications. In addition to literary works, all political, economic, legal, scientific, educational... and other books and newspapers are included in the introduction, but books and newspapers with no connection will not be introduced.

(2) For books, only recent works by new domestic and foreign authors and attachments related to the text are allowed.

(3) Articles on textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(4) Pictures and photographs are limited to those related to the text.

(5) Each article should not exceed 3,000 words.

(6) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.
